\doxysubsection{Detailed Description}
\subsubsection*{template$<$typename Expression\+Type, int Direction$>$\newline
class Eigen\+::\+Vectorwise\+Op$<$ Expression\+Type, Direction $>$}
Pseudo expression providing broadcasting and partial reduction operations. 


\begin{DoxyTemplParams}{Template Parameters}
{\em Expression\+Type} & the type of the object on which to do partial reductions \\
\hline
{\em Direction} & indicates whether to operate on columns (\doxylink{group__enums_ggad49a7b3738e273eb00932271b36127f7addca718e0564723df21d61b94b1198be}{Vertical}) or rows (\doxylink{group__enums_ggad49a7b3738e273eb00932271b36127f7aae8a16b3b9272683c1162915f6d892be}{Horizontal})\\
\hline
\end{DoxyTemplParams}
This class represents a pseudo expression with broadcasting and partial reduction features. It is the return type of \doxylink{classEigen_1_1DenseBase_a978724c07b70cb9b8fdef67a4de08788}{Dense\+Base\+::colwise()} and \doxylink{classEigen_1_1DenseBase_af9662cd704ffc16c5b88c7b2d331576f}{Dense\+Base\+::rowwise()} and most of the time this is the only way it is explicitly used.

To understand the logic of rowwise/colwise expression, let\textquotesingle{}s consider a generic case {\ttfamily A.\+colwise().foo()} where {\ttfamily foo} is any method of {\ttfamily \doxylink{classEigen_1_1VectorwiseOp}{Vectorwise\+Op}}. This expression is equivalent to applying {\ttfamily foo()} to each column of {\ttfamily A} and then re-\/assemble the outputs in a matrix expression\+: 
\begin{DoxyCode}{0}
\DoxyCodeLine{[A.col(0).foo(),\ A.col(1).foo(),\ ...,\ A.col(A.cols()-\/1).foo()]\ }

\end{DoxyCode}


Example\+: 
\begin{DoxyCodeInclude}{0}

\end{DoxyCodeInclude}
 Output\+: 
\begin{DoxyVerbInclude}
\end{DoxyVerbInclude}


The \doxylink{classEigen_1_1VectorwiseOp_abbf3325f535ac011ed61f14ed4330618}{begin()} and \doxylink{classEigen_1_1VectorwiseOp_a9d189042b8322e40772d41c63b9d3bb5}{end()} methods are obviously exceptions to the previous rule as they return STL-\/compatible begin/end iterators to the rows or columns of the nested expression. Typical use cases include for-\/range-\/loop and calls to STL algorithms\+:

Example\+: 
\begin{DoxyCodeInclude}{0}

\end{DoxyCodeInclude}
 Output\+: 
\begin{DoxyVerbInclude}
\end{DoxyVerbInclude}


For a partial reduction on an empty input, some rules apply. For the sake of clarity, let\textquotesingle{}s consider a vertical reduction\+:
\begin{DoxyItemize}
\item If the number of columns is zero, then a 1x0 row-\/major vector expression is returned.
\item Otherwise, if the number of rows is zero, then
\begin{DoxyItemize}
\item a row vector of zeros is returned for sum-\/like reductions (sum, squared\+Norm, norm, etc.)
\item a row vector of ones is returned for a product reduction (e.\+g., {\ttfamily Matrix\+Xd(n,0).colwise().\doxylink{classEigen_1_1VectorwiseOp_a6863499c3e7ea8635784376806abcf9f}{prod()}})
\item an assert is triggered for all other reductions (min\+Coeff,max\+Coeff,redux(bin\+\_\+op))
\end{DoxyItemize}
\end{DoxyItemize}

\begin{DoxySeeAlso}{See also}
\doxylink{classEigen_1_1DenseBase_a978724c07b70cb9b8fdef67a4de08788}{Dense\+Base\+::colwise()}, \doxylink{classEigen_1_1DenseBase_af9662cd704ffc16c5b88c7b2d331576f}{Dense\+Base\+::rowwise()}, class \doxylink{classEigen_1_1PartialReduxExpr}{Partial\+Redux\+Expr} 
\end{DoxySeeAlso}

\begin{DoxyReturn}{Returns}
a row (or column) vector expression of the norm of each column (or row) of the referenced expression, using Blue\textquotesingle{}s algorithm. This is a vector with real entries, even if the original matrix has complex entries.
\end{DoxyReturn}

\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{count()}{count()}\hspace{0.1cm}{\footnotesize\ttfamily [1/2]}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily \label{classEigen_1_1VectorwiseOp_abf7ae4a00d195d06d46ad6c269d8508f} 
template$<$typename Expression\+Type , int Direction$>$ \\
\mbox{\hyperlink{eigen_2Eigen_2src_2Core_2util_2Macros_8h_a9efec3cfd22b9a33bead9c6718d128da}{EIGEN\+\_\+\+DEVICE\+\_\+\+FUNC}} const \mbox{\hyperlink{classEigen_1_1VectorwiseOp_aa5442e5ad28b7834a67a0c894f508bde}{Count\+Return\+Type}} \mbox{\hyperlink{classEigen_1_1VectorwiseOp}{Eigen\+::\+Vectorwise\+Op}}$<$ Expression\+Type, Direction $>$\+::count (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}{}{}\end{DoxyParamCaption}) const\hspace{0.3cm}{\ttfamily [inline]}}

\begin{DoxyReturn}{Returns}
a row (or column) vector expression representing the number of {\ttfamily true} coefficients of each respective column (or row). This expression can be assigned to a vector whose entries have the same type as is used to index entries of the original matrix; for dense matrices, this is {\ttfamily std\+::ptrdiff\+\_\+t} .
\end{DoxyReturn}
Example\+: 
\begin{DoxyCodeInclude}{0}

\end{DoxyCodeInclude}

\Hypertarget{classEigen_1_1VectorwiseOp_a9ae3feb2723628a3bcff6eabda2fa77d}\index{Eigen::VectorwiseOp$<$ ExpressionType, Direction $>$@{Eigen::VectorwiseOp$<$ ExpressionType, Direction $>$}!hypotNorm@{hypotNorm}}
\index{hypotNorm@{hypotNorm}!Eigen::VectorwiseOp$<$ ExpressionType, Direction $>$@{Eigen::VectorwiseOp$<$ ExpressionType, Direction $>$}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{hypotNorm()}{hypotNorm()}\hspace{0.1cm}{\footnotesize\ttfamily [1/2]}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily \label{classEigen_1_1VectorwiseOp_a9ae3feb2723628a3bcff6eabda2fa77d} 
template$<$typename Expression\+Type , int Direction$>$ \\
\mbox{\hyperlink{eigen_2Eigen_2src_2Core_2util_2Macros_8h_a9efec3cfd22b9a33bead9c6718d128da}{EIGEN\+\_\+\+DEVICE\+\_\+\+FUNC}} const \mbox{\hyperlink{classEigen_1_1VectorwiseOp_a1ee82a67331beef99db0cd229f135124}{Hypot\+Norm\+Return\+Type}} \mbox{\hyperlink{classEigen_1_1VectorwiseOp}{Eigen\+::\+Vectorwise\+Op}}$<$ Expression\+Type, Direction $>$\+::hypot\+Norm (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}{}{}\end{DoxyParamCaption}) const\hspace{0.3cm}{\ttfamily [inline]}}

\begin{DoxyReturn}{Returns}
a row (or column) vector expression of the norm of each column (or row) of the referenced expression, avoiding underflow and overflow using a concatenation of hypot() calls. This is a vector with real entries, even if the original matrix has complex entries.
\end{DoxyReturn}

template$<$typename Expression\+Type , int Direction$>$ \\
\mbox{\hyperlink{eigen_2Eigen_2src_2Core_2util_2Macros_8h_a9efec3cfd22b9a33bead9c6718d128da}{EIGEN\+\_\+\+DEVICE\+\_\+\+FUNC}} const \mbox{\hyperlink{classEigen_1_1VectorwiseOp_a7d9d3dc3c9fa001768ddf9f0ba5a700d}{Max\+Coeff\+Return\+Type}} \mbox{\hyperlink{classEigen_1_1VectorwiseOp}{Eigen\+::\+Vectorwise\+Op}}$<$ Expression\+Type, Direction $>$\+::max\+Coeff (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}{}{}\end{DoxyParamCaption}) const\hspace{0.3cm}{\ttfamily [inline]}}

\begin{DoxyReturn}{Returns}
a row (or column) vector expression of the largest coefficient of each column (or row) of the referenced expression.
\end{DoxyReturn}
\begin{DoxyWarning}{Warning}
the size along the reduction direction must be strictly positive, otherwise an assertion is triggered.

the result is undefined if {\ttfamily \texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*}this} contains NaN.
\end{DoxyWarning}

{\footnotesize\ttfamily \label{classEigen_1_1VectorwiseOp_a05f6f60662c06b4987e7eaf747a032c0} 
template$<$typename Expression\+Type , int Direction$>$ \\
\mbox{\hyperlink{eigen_2Eigen_2src_2Core_2util_2Macros_8h_a9efec3cfd22b9a33bead9c6718d128da}{EIGEN\+\_\+\+DEVICE\+\_\+\+FUNC}} const \mbox{\hyperlink{classEigen_1_1VectorwiseOp_a6aa216679ce7b5f964b7528e9053bb64}{Min\+Coeff\+Return\+Type}} \mbox{\hyperlink{classEigen_1_1VectorwiseOp}{Eigen\+::\+Vectorwise\+Op}}$<$ Expression\+Type, Direction $>$\+::min\+Coeff (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}{}{}\end{DoxyParamCaption}) const\hspace{0.3cm}{\ttfamily [inline]}}

\begin{DoxyReturn}{Returns}
a row (or column) vector expression of the smallest coefficient of each column (or row) of the referenced expression.
\end{DoxyReturn}
\begin{DoxyWarning}{Warning}
the size along the reduction direction must be strictly positive, otherwise an assertion is triggered.

the result is undefined if {\ttfamily \texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*}this} contains NaN.
\end{DoxyWarning}

template$<$typename Expression\+Type , int Direction$>$ \\
template$<$typename Binary\+Op $>$ \\
\mbox{\hyperlink{eigen_2Eigen_2src_2Core_2util_2Macros_8h_a9efec3cfd22b9a33bead9c6718d128da}{EIGEN\+\_\+\+DEVICE\+\_\+\+FUNC}} const \mbox{\hyperlink{structEigen_1_1VectorwiseOp_1_1ReduxReturnType}{Redux\+Return\+Type}}$<$ Binary\+Op $>$\+::\+Type \mbox{\hyperlink{classEigen_1_1VectorwiseOp}{Eigen\+::\+Vectorwise\+Op}}$<$ Expression\+Type, Direction $>$\+::redux (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{const Binary\+Op \&}]{func}{ = {\ttfamily BinaryOp()}}\end{DoxyParamCaption}) const\hspace{0.3cm}{\ttfamily [inline]}}

\begin{DoxyReturn}{Returns}
a row or column vector expression of {\ttfamily \texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*}this} reduxed by {\itshape func} 
\end{DoxyReturn}
The template parameter {\itshape Binary\+Op} is the type of the functor of the custom redux operator. Note that func must be an associative operator.

\begin{DoxyWarning}{Warning}
the size along the reduction direction must be strictly positive, otherwise an assertion is triggered.
\end{DoxyWarning}

\Hypertarget{classEigen_1_1VectorwiseOp_a2bd419527acce58e9e813a5af654b81c}\index{Eigen::VectorwiseOp$<$ ExpressionType, Direction $>$@{Eigen::VectorwiseOp$<$ ExpressionType, Direction $>$}!reverseInPlace@{reverseInPlace}}
\index{reverseInPlace@{reverseInPlace}!Eigen::VectorwiseOp$<$ ExpressionType, Direction $>$@{Eigen::VectorwiseOp$<$ ExpressionType, Direction $>$}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{reverseInPlace()}{reverseInPlace()}\hspace{0.1cm}{\footnotesize\ttfamily [1/2]}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily \label{classEigen_1_1VectorwiseOp_a2bd419527acce58e9e813a5af654b81c} 
template$<$typename Expression\+Type , int Direction$>$ \\
\mbox{\hyperlink{eigen_2Eigen_2src_2Core_2util_2Macros_8h_a9efec3cfd22b9a33bead9c6718d128da}{EIGEN\+\_\+\+DEVICE\+\_\+\+FUNC}} void \mbox{\hyperlink{classEigen_1_1VectorwiseOp}{Eigen\+::\+Vectorwise\+Op}}$<$ Expression\+Type, Direction $>$\+::reverse\+In\+Place (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}{}{}\end{DoxyParamCaption})\hspace{0.3cm}{\ttfamily [inline]}}

This is the "{}in place"{} version of \doxylink{classEigen_1_1VectorwiseOp_a058b821b65e2e27839853d9a25b0216c}{Vectorwise\+Op\+::reverse}\+: it reverses each column or row of {\ttfamily \texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*}this}.

In most cases it is probably better to simply use the reversed expression of a matrix. However, when reversing the matrix data itself is really needed, then this "{}in-\/place"{} version is probably the right choice because it provides the following additional benefits\+:
\begin{DoxyItemize}
\item less error prone\+: doing the same operation with .\doxylink{classEigen_1_1VectorwiseOp_a094915725d604015221205e8c4ccb993}{reverse()} requires special care\+: 
\begin{DoxyCode}{0}
\DoxyCodeLine{m\ =\ m.reverse().eval();\ }

\end{DoxyCode}

\item this API enables reverse operations without the need for a temporary
\end{DoxyItemize}

{\footnotesize\ttfamily \label{classEigen_1_1VectorwiseOp_a6f23ba41822436d3176d718596be8fd0} 
template$<$typename Expression\+Type , int Direction$>$ \\
\mbox{\hyperlink{eigen_2Eigen_2src_2Core_2util_2Macros_8h_a9efec3cfd22b9a33bead9c6718d128da}{EIGEN\+\_\+\+DEVICE\+\_\+\+FUNC}} const \mbox{\hyperlink{classEigen_1_1VectorwiseOp_a3220598f863402b7176a6d543aacd717}{Squared\+Norm\+Return\+Type}} \mbox{\hyperlink{classEigen_1_1VectorwiseOp}{Eigen\+::\+Vectorwise\+Op}}$<$ Expression\+Type, Direction $>$\+::squared\+Norm (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}{}{}\end{DoxyParamCaption}) const\hspace{0.3cm}{\ttfamily [inline]}}

\begin{DoxyReturn}{Returns}
a row (or column) vector expression of the squared norm of each column (or row) of the referenced expression. This is a vector with real entries, even if the original matrix has complex entries.
\end{DoxyReturn}
